[<hi rend="ital">A religious visit to the sacred places at Mekkeh, with the performance of the ceremony of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الإِحْرَام</foreign>,] <hi rend="ital">the circuiting round the Kaabeh, and the going to and fro between Es-Safà and El-Marweh:</hi>

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30517-2" target="عُمُرٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30520"/></foreign>, (K, &amp;c.,) [used as <pb n="2155"/> simple substs., or abstract ns., in which case the second is more common than the first, except in forms of swearing, in which the former is used, and the third is more chaste than the second,] signify <hi rend="ital">Life;</hi> (Msb, K;) [the <hi rend="ital">age to which the life extends;</hi>] the <hi rend="ital">period during which the body is inhabited by life:</hi> so that it denotes less than <foreign lang="ar">بَقَآءٌ</foreign>: wherefore the latter is [frequently] used as an attribute of God; but <foreign lang="ar">عمر</foreign> is seldom used as such: (Er-Rághib, B:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَعْمَارٌ</foreign>. (K.) You say   
      <foreign lang="ar">أَطَالَ ٱللّٰهُ <ref cref="n30517-3" target="عُمُرَكَ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَمْرَكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">May God prolong thy life</hi>]. (S, O.) In a form of swearing, <foreign lang="ar">عَمْر</foreign> only is used. (S.) [In a case of this kind, when <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> is not prefixed to it, it is in the accus. case, as will be shown and expl. below: but when <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> is prefixed to it, it is in the nom.] You say <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُكَ لَأَفْعَلَنَّ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">By thy life, I will assuredly do</hi> [such a thing].       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30517-5" target="لَعَمَرِى" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">by my life,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">by my religion.</hi> (K.) <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُكَ</foreign> is an inchoative, of which the enunciative, <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُقْسِمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">that by which I swear,</hi> so that the entire phrase means <hi rend="ital">thy life is that by which I swear,</hi>] is understood; therefore it is in the nom. case: (IJ, TA:) or the complete phrase is <foreign lang="ar">وَعَمْرِكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَلَعَمْرُكَ عَظِيمٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">by thy life,</hi> &amp;c.: <hi rend="ital">and thy life is of great account</hi>]. (Fr, as related by A'Obeyd.) You say also <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُ أَبِيكَ الخَيْرَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">الخَيْرِ</foreign>; the former meaning <hi rend="ital">By thy father's instituting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">promoting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">keeping to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">observing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">regarding, what is good;</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الخير</foreign> being the objective complement of <foreign lang="ar">عمر</foreign>, from <foreign lang="ar">عَمَرَ الخَيْرَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">عَمُرَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَمْرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عِمَارَةٌ</foreign>; [see 1;] but in the latter case, <foreign lang="ar">الخَيْرِ</foreign> is an epithet added to <foreign lang="ar">أَبِيكَ</foreign> [so that the meaning is <hi rend="ital">by the life of thy good father</hi>]. (AHeyth, Az, O, TA.) [See also art. <foreign lang="ar">خير</foreign>.] You also say <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">By the everlasting existence of God;</hi> (S, O, K;) <foreign lang="ar">عمر</foreign> being here in the nom. case as an inchoative, with <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> prefixed to it as a corroborative of the inchoative state: the enunciative is understood; the complete phrase being <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُ ٱللّٰهِ قَسَمِى</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُقْسِمُ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the everlasting existence of God is my oath,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">that by which I swear</hi>]. (S, O.) This expression is forbidden in a trad., (K,) because <foreign lang="ar">عَمْرٌ</foreign> [properly] means the life of the body: (TA:) [but] <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">إِلٰهِكَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">By the everlasting existence of thy God,</hi> occurs in a trad. (TA.) When you do not prefix <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign>, you make it to be in the accus. case, as an inf. n.: thus you say, <foreign lang="ar">عمْرَ ٱللّٰهِ مَا فَعَلْتُ كَذَا</foreign> (S, O, K) I swear <hi rend="ital">by the everlasting existence of God, I did not so:</hi> (S, O:) and <foreign lang="ar">عَمْرَكَ ٱللّٰهَ مَا</foreign>
